12:49:39","updatedTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:39","title":"How a designer who upholsters furniture by hand managed to grow her business in a pandemic","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/nicole-crowder-upholstery-designer-furniture-2020-11","description":"<div style=\"position:relative; overflow:hidden; padding-bottom:56.25%\">\n<iframe src=\"https://cdn.jwplayer.com/players/KL8EVzYT-jZbcmOYf.html\"\nwidth=\"100%\" height=\"100%\" frameborder=\"0\" scrolling=\"auto\" title=\"How a designer who upholsters furniture by hand managed to grow her business in a pandemic\"\nstyle=\"position:absolute;\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n</div><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Designer Nicole Crowder uses traditional techniques and her own unique taste to upholster furniture by hand.</li>\n<li>Her business has grown, despite the pandemic, as people in her hometown of Washington and beyond discover her.</li>\n<li>Crowder charges between $900 and $2,200 for each custom upholstery piece, and she's starting to make her own original pieces.</li>\n<li><strong><a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/BusinessInsiderToday/\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\">View more episodes of Business Insider Today on Facebook.</a></strong></li>\n</ul><p>Every piece of furniture tells a story for Nicole Crowder.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://www.nicolecrowderupholstery.com/\">Washington, DC, designer</a> hand-makes custom upholstery using traditional techniques, even though most furniture nowadays is mass-produced in factories.</p><p>\"I think a lot about preservation, you know. How do you take care of something?\" Crowder told Business Insider Today. \"And I don't have children, so I think my furniture has become my children. It's something that I really have to take my time nurturing from start to finish.\"</p><p>Crowder started her upholstery business in her small Washington apartment four years ago, but eventually had to move to bigger and bigger spaces.</p><p>Despite the pandemic, her orders have grown this year. She now hires seamstresses and a driver, and has contracts with hotels and restaurants around the city.</p><p>\"Within six months, just the amount of work that I was being offered had increased exponentially, I think largely because folks were becoming more familiar with what I was doing,\" she said. \"You know, you have your own stamp on the work. There's this very specific kind of style and aesthetic that I have that I think people were interested in.\"</p><p>Crowder charges anywhere from $900 to $2,200 and has worked on 60 pieces of furniture so far this year.&#160;</p><p>As her business expands, she said she's now starting to work on original products, including meditation pillows.</p><p>\"One thing that I really enjoyed about the way that I have scaled is very intentional about it,\" she said. \"I take the time to really ask myself certain questions about, is this something I meant to do? Is this the way that I want to grow? Does this feel good? Do I have the bandwidth to take it on?\"</p><p>\"I am in the midst of designing my own custom furniture for the first time, which I'm incredibly excited about. And that just feels like a dream.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/nicole-crowder-upholstery-designer-furniture-2020-11'>Business Fauci's \"upbeat\" tone on the coronavirus pandemic since Election Day.</li>\n<li>Fauci on Tuesday&#160;predicted that a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fauci-covid-19-vaccine-april-pfizer-healthcare-elderly-vulnerable-2020-11\">vaccine will hopefully be available </a>to Americans by April, following drugmaker Pfizer's positive news about its coronavirus vaccine candidate.</li>\n<li>\"Well maybe he's cheered up because of the election,\" Atlas said.</li>\n<li>Since Atlas joined the White House coronavirus task force, tensions between him and other members, including Fauci, have escalated.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Scott Atlas, a coronavirus adviser to President Donald Trump, slammed Dr. Anthony Fauci on Tuesday as \"a political animal,\" hours after the country's top infectious disease expert provided his latest verdict on the state of the pandemic.&#160;</p><p>Atlas made the comments during a nightly appearance on <a href=\"https://video.foxnews.com/v/6208873994001#sp=show-clips\">Fox News with host Laura Ingraham</a>, who claimed Fauci has taken on an \"upbeat\" tone toward the virus since Election Day.</p><p>She compared a clip of Fauci from late October in which he said the United States likely<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fauci-coronavirus-us-wont-see-semblances-of-normality-until-2022-2020-10\">&#160;won't see \"semblances of normality\"</a> until 2022 to an interview of him on Tuesday when he predicted that a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fauci-covid-19-vaccine-april-pfizer-healthcare-elderly-vulnerable-2020-11\">vaccine will hopefully be available </a>to Americans by April.&#160;</p><p>\"There's all kinds of prognostications that were made, all negative, all to undermine what the reality of the timelines were, all to undermine the president,\" Atlas said. \"Once you do that sort of thing and make yourself a political animal basically, you lose your credibility.\"</p><p>However, Fauci's remarks on a COVID-19 vaccine came after drugmaker Pfizer <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-coronavirus-vaccine-success-plans-for-emergency-approval-fda-2020-9?r=US&IR=TIR=T\">announced on Monday</a> that its coronavirus vaccine candidate completed its final stage of clinical trials with a 90% efficacy rate.&#160;</p><p>\"This is very good news looking forward,\" Fauci said <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fauci-pfizer-vaccine-90-percent-efficacy-rate-extraordinary-2020-11\">on Monday</a>, adding that the results are \"extraordinary\" and \"have a major impact on everything that we do with regard to COVID.\"</p><p>Still, Atlas pushed back on Fauci, adding to a string of baseless attacks from the White House that public health officials and pharmaceutical companies are working against Trump to harm his political standing. Trump has <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/donald-trump-claims-dr-fauci-is-a-democrat-no-evidence-2020-10\">falsely accused</a> Fauci of being a Democrat and called <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/anthony-fauci-donald-trump-coronavirus-restrictions-election-2020-10\">him a \"disaster,\"</a> as the two have often not seen eye-to-eye on the federal coronavirus response.&#160;</p><p>\"Well maybe [Fauci's] cheered up because of the election,\" Atlas said.</p><p>Atlas also repeated an <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-pfizer-covid-19-vaccine-conspiracy-theory-delay-election-day-2020-11\">unfounded claim</a> from Trump that Pfizer deliberately withheld coronavirus vaccine data from the public until after Election Day. Trump <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/2020-election-results\">lost the election</a> last week to President-elect Joe Biden, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/2020-election-results\">Insider and Decision Desk HQ</a> projected on November 6.&#160;</p><p>Atlas frequently appeared on Fox News echoing the president's views on the pandemic before the Trump administration tapped him to join the White House coronavirus task force. Since his arrival in August, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/scott-atlas-hits-back-critics-questioning-science-fauci-redfield-2020-10\">tensions between</a> him and Fauci, as well as task force coordinator Dr. Deborah Birx, have escalated based on conflicting views on how to tackle the virus.</p><p>Atlas, who has no background in epidemiology, has <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/coronavirus-adviser-is-pushing-white-house-to-adopt-herd-immunity-2020-8\">reportedly tried</a> to push a controversial \"herd immunity\" strategy, which Fauci and Birx have argued could potentially lead to higher death rates. A senior administration official previously told <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trump-coronavirus-scott-atlas-herd-immunity/2020/08/30/925e68fe-e93b-11ea-970a-64c73a1c2392_story.html\">The Washington Post</a> that Atlas has positioned himself as an \"anti-Dr. Fauci.\"</p><p>Another Trump ally, Steve Bannon, also recently attacked Fauci and&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/steve-bannon-banned-twitter-fauci-and-wrays-heads-on-pikes-2020-11\">called for the beheading</a> of him and other government officials.&#160;</p><p>Fauci responded in <a href=\"https://www.abc.net.au/7.30/dr-anthony-fauci-about-covid-19-in-the-us/12874036\">an interview on Wednesday</a> that it's been \"very stressful\" helping manage the pandemic under the Trump administration.&#160;</p><p>\"When you have public figures like Bannon calling for your beheading, that's really kind of unusual,\" he said.&#160;\"But I've gotten through it by really focusing like a laser beam on exactly what my goal is. I'm a scientist and I'm a physician.\"</p><p>\"People calling for you to be beheaded, fired, thrown in the fire pit, or whatever, that's just noise. You don't pay attention to that,\" he added.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Seddiq)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fac0c2eb09abb0018625f51?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn87@2020_1/2020/11/12/04-50-03-438_dd162360e8ed6599.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn11@2020_1/2020/11/12/04-50-05-069_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=U_zifEbP_gg:35A8gyskwn4:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn20@2020_3/2020/11/12/04-50-07-682_18999bb34cc65f48.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=U_zifEbP_gg:35A8gyskwn4:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn88@2020_6/2020/11/12/04-49-56-394_8b8346d8ae0efec9.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn48@2020_5/2020/11/12/04-49-59-767_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=U_zifEbP_gg:35A8gyskwn4:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn51@2020_3/2020/11/12/04-50-04-472_8aa42ce1d9783e3b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/U_zifEbP_gg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn32@2020_1/2020/11/12/04-50-03-932_abff236a652aa1ed.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605156579271},{"createdTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:39","updatedTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:39","title":"Of course Trump is trying to burn it all down. What else did you expect?","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-trumpworld-sore-losers-election-biden-expected-dont-panic-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fac10ecb09abb0018625f70?format=jpeg\" alt=\"donald trump rally\" height=\"1463\" width=\"1950\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>President Donald Trump was always going to go kicking and screaming from the White House\n<p class=\"copyright\">Getty</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>President Trump's refusal to admit that he lost the 2020 election to President-elect Joe Biden has made things extremely stressful here in the United States.</li>\n<li>But at least everyone is behaving exactly as expected.</li>\n<li>Trump is in denial, and the GOP is talking loud, but the Trump campaign's legal challenges are thin.</li>\n<li>This feels terrible because we're in it, and it may very well do longterm damage to our democracy, but no one can say we're being surprised here.</li>\n<li>This is an opinion column. The thoughts expressed are those of the author.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The days since former Vice President Joe Biden won the 2020 Presidential election have been intense, aggravating and long — but at least everyone is behaving exactly as expected.</p><p>President Donald Trump is refusing to concede, just like we <a href=\"https://www.theatlantic.com/ideas/archive/2020/10/lazy-cowards-dont-start-civil-wars/616720/\">all knew he would</a>. He's golfing and seething and tweeting that the election was \"rigged.\" At the same time his public presidential <a href=\"https://t.co/JUEEmXf77J?amp=1\">schedule is empty</a>, and even though coronavirus cases are hitting record levels, he has not addressed the public in about a week. He <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/donald-trump-ghost-america-losing-election-joe-biden-inauguration-2020-11\">doesn't have the guts</a>.</p><p>Naturally, the Trump administration is recalcitrant as well. It is refusing to help Biden's team with the transition. It is reshuffling the Department of Defense in a way that is disturbing the <a href=\"https://twitter.com/GenMhayden/status/1326346254092267520\">national security community</a>. And — just to add some pettiness to all of this — it is threatening to fire anyone on the inside <a href=\"https://www.vanityfair.com/news/2020/11/john-mcentee-trump-admin-new-jobs\">who starts looking for a job.</a> Harrowing, but again, totally expected from these people.</p><p>Senate Majority Leader Mitch McConnell wants to win two special elections in Georgia in early January which will decide which party controls the Senate. So he's adding fuel to Trump's fire in an attempt to turn out the base, refusing to reject Trump's baseless legal challenges to the election, and further eroding America's faith in the democratic process. This could have a long term negative impact on our democracy, but that's fine for McConnell — which shouldn't surprise anyone.&#160;</p><p>Secretary of State Mike Pompeo — who is being investigated for <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2020/11/10/state-department-watchdog-pompeo-435753\">abusing his office</a> and spent this spring&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pompeo-spreads-wuhan-lab-coronavirus-conspiracy-get-trump-attention-2020-5\">spreading the lie</a> that the coronavirus escaped from a lab in Wuhan — is being a bully. No surprise there. On Tuesday he crowed that we would have smooth transition to \"<a href=\"https://t.co/Gc9y1RivmE?amp=1\">a second Trump administration</a>,\" but now he seems to be <a href=\"https://twitter.com/atrupar/status/1326309985031249926\">walking that back at bit</a>. Bullies often do that upon confrontation.</p><p>Attorney General Bill Barr — known for using legalese to make his <a href=\"https://www.cbsnews.com/news/attorney-general-william-barr-order-expand-white-house-perimeter-protesters/\">aggression as passive</a> as possible — wrote a letter allowing US Attorneys to \"pursue substantial allegations of voter fraud.\" It's unclear to legal experts whether it's a move that has any real teeth, but the head of the <a href=\"https://www.npr.org/sections/live-updates-2020-election-results/2020/11/10/933395215/head-of-doj-s-election-crimes-unit-steps-down-after-barr-oks-election-inquiries\">DOJ's Election Crimes Unit</a> stepped down shortly thereafter.</p><p>Jared Kushner is <a href=\"https://twitter.com/crampell/status/1325504043985350658\">outsourcing</a> the brutal task of getting his father-in-law to accept reality to friends (much like the coronavirus response). And his wife Ivanka Trump — America's duchess of dissociation — is <a href=\"https://twitter.com/IvankaTrump\">tweeting</a> as if nothing is wrong, like she just touched down here from another planet or something. All of this is extremely on brand for everyone.</p><p>But that predictability doesn't make it any less stressful in the moment, I understand that. Even though election officials around the country insist there was no <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/11/10/us/politics/voting-fraud.html?action=click&module=Spotlight&pgtype=HomepageHomepage\">widespread malfeasance</a>, even though Trump's legal challenges look really thin, this tension could drag on until Inauguration Day on January 20.</p><p>There's a lot that could go wrong between now and then. Coronavirus cases are spiking in what experts are calling \"the most deadly\" phase of the virus. Changes at the Defense Department have some worried that our country could be vulnerable while Trump pitches his fit. Plus, Congress is supposed to be negotiating a coronavirus aid package and this aggression is not good for coming to agreements.</p><p>Over on Wall Street, the CBOE volatility index (better known as the VIX) started spiking on Monday even as stocks rallied on the news that Pfizer developed a COVID-19 vaccine with 90% efficacy. The market knows that even though the election is over, Trump's refusal to accept that reality will make it a bumpy ride to 2021.</p><p>It's going to be wretched, but we all knew this was coming. No one around Trump has come to their senses, there are no heroes on the GOP's side, and while it's nice that First Lady Melania Trump is <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/melania-trump-urging-trump-concede-biden-election-cnn-2020-11\">urging her husband to accept</a> his loss let's be honest — she's been dying to leave the White House anyway.&#160; Everyone is behaving exactly as horribly as we expected they would. Let these appalling people be themselves, and keep your eye on January 20.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a They'll learn plenty of new recipes and cooking techniques &#8212; and you might even get to taste the fruits of their labor one day.&#160;</p>\n\tA nice candle with a reusable vessel\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d6408ca2e22af045e366295?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Lafco, $65\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lafco</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><strong><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B003ZA753C/ref=as_li_tl?ie=UTF8&#38;tag=biip_102618_in-laws-gifts-20&#38;camp=1789&#38;creative=9325&#38;linkCode=as2&#38;creativeASIN=B003ZA753C&#38;linkId=268465b0dae1d4471155ab9cd81cab9f\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow nofollow nofollow\">Lafco Library Candle, $65, available at Amazon</a></strong></h3><p>A nice candle is always a welcomed gift. These ones are made to embody the scents of common places, including rooms in the house. The best part of these candles, though, is that they'll be able to reuse the hand-blown glass vessel once the candle has burned down. All they have to do is put it in the freezer when the wax runs down, pop it out with a knife, and run it through the dishwasher. Our editor uses hers for everything from cotton swabs to serving snacks.</p>\n\tAn Airbnb gift card for in-laws who love to travel\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5d6401082e22af02ae6bcfd8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"airbnb, $100&#43;\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Airbnb Instagram</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><strong><a href=\"http://zola.pxf.io/c/196318/584112/9631?subId1=biip_102618_in-laws-gifts&#38;u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.zola.com%2Fshop%2Fbrand%2Fairbnb\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow\">Airbnb Gift Card, $100 - $500, available at Zola</a></strong></h3><p>A tangible gift is great, but so is the gift of an unforgettable experience. 12:49:39","updatedTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:39","title":"These 6 ecommerce companies will continue to thrive in a post-pandemic world, Stifel says","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/ecommerce-companies-stocks-thrive-post-pandemic-world-stifel-says-2020-11","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f808b224c3b2e0019bba2be?format=jpeg\" alt=\"woman paying on phone online shopping\" height=\"1060\" width=\"2121\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Tashdique Mehtaj Ahmed/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>E-commerce companies have thrived amid the COVID-19 pandemic as more people have shifted to online shopping to avoid physical trips to the store.</strong></li><li><strong>But the accelerated adoption of e-commerce is set to stall as the world gets back to normal once a COVID-19 vaccine is made widely available in 2021, according to a note from Stifel.</strong></li><li><strong>An initial shift by consumers to services and experience spending over material goods will likely present a headwind for e-commerce companies over the next six to nine months, but many companies will continue to benefit from the positive trends set during the pandemic.</strong></li><li><strong>These are the 6 e-commerce companies that are set to thrive in a post-pandemic world, according to Stifel.</strong></li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/international?r=US&IR=T?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingesttm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong>Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li></ul><hr><p>No group of companies have benefited more from the COVID-19 pandemic than e-commerce companies, and there may still be ground left to gain.&#160;</p><p>The sector experienced a massive surge in business amid the pandemic as consumers shifted to online shopping in order to limit physical trips to traditional retail stores. In the second quarter of 2020, online&#160;shopping surged 44% compared to the prior year and represented more than 20% of all retail sales, according to <a href=\"https://www.census.gov/retail/mrts/www/data/pdf/ec_current.pdf\">data from the department of commerce.</a></p><p>But with this week's news of a successful <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pfizer-coronavirus-vaccine-success-plans-for-emergency-approval-fda-2020-9\">COVID-19 vaccine being developed by Pfizer and BioNtech,</a> a return to normal is likely over the next six to nine months, according to Stifel.</p><p>In a note on Monday, the Wall Street firm said it expects the next three quarter to be rough for e-commerce stocks \"as investors begin to asses the sustainability of underlying trends amplified by COVID-19 and the approaching difficult comps starting in 2Q 2021.\"</p><p>But Stifel remains \"incredibly optimistic\" on these 6 e-commerce stocks despite a six-to-nine month headwind ahead, according to the note.</p><h2><strong>1. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/amzn-stock\">Amazon</a></strong></h2><p>\"Amazon has been a primary beneficiary of the pandemic given the increased penetration of e-commerce , helped by higher online grocery and consumables spend, and the continued dislocation in offline retail. Under a recovery scenario, we see Amazon continuing to benefit from these developments,\" Stifel said.</p><p>Prime users are continuing to shop at a greater frequency, and Stifel argues this trend is likely to remain in place given how sticky Amazon's Prime ecosystem is.&#160;</p><p>On top of that, Amazon's deep investments into the cloud will likely continue to bear fruit in 2021 given that the company highlighted an increase in the backlog of multiyear deals on its third quarter earnings call.</p><h2><strong>2. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/ebay-stock\">eBay</a></strong></h2><p>\"Despite our expectations for decelerating volume growth, we believe management is focused on improving the core marketplace business and is developing new experiences to support growth and retain some of the new and reactivated customers brought to the platform in recent months. eBay has recently announced new initiatives in authentication and the development of a platform for refurbished items with some exclusive brand partnerships,\" Stifel said.</p><p>Stifel expects initiatives from eBay's new CEO, improvements to the buyer/seller experience, and the business opportunity from managed payments to support better-than-expected volume and revenue growth in the coming quarters, according to the note.</p><h2><strong>3. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/etsy-stock\">Etsy</a></strong></h2><p>\"We expect near-term volatility in shares as the company enters 2021, and expect a sizable deceleration in GMS growth under a vaccine scenario in the coming quarters. 2021 presents challenging comps in 2Q and 2H, compounded by a decline in facemask sales as the health crisis hopefully subsides,\" Stifel said.<strong><br></strong></p><p>Despite a challenging setup in 2021, \"we believe Etsy will continue to benefit from the meaningful increase in awareness and engagement brought on by the pandemic,\" Stifel said.</p><p>\"We would be buyers of extended weakness and believe ongoing investments in product improvements will support retention, though note that it will likely take many quarters for this dynamic to be fully realized,\" Stifel concluded.</p><h2><strong>4. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/nflx-stock\">Netflix</a></strong></h2><p>\"Netflix's business has benefited from the pandemic in several ways: some subscriber pull-forward effect, competitive consolidation, and content spend efficiencies.&#160;Thematic de-risking could lead to further near-term consolidation in shares, while risk such as the subscriber digestion period and price increase implementation will likely remain on the radar. We are comfortable with the long-term growth opportunity and could see an opportunity in Netflix shares should sentiment swing too far in the negative direction in the coming months/quarters,\" Stifel said.</p><h2><strong>5. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/pton-stock\">Peloton</a></strong></h2><p>\"From $100, we see room for a three-year double,\" Stifel said.</p><p>\"Peloton has been one of the marquee beneficiaries of pandemic-related shifts in consumer behavior and discretionary spending. The immediate reaction in Peloton shares on the Pfizer vaccine news makes sense, with shares down -20%,\" Stifel noted.</p><p>\"However, here is why we continue to recommend shares: we view the fitness industry as forever changed. Yes, consumers may gradually return to gyms, yoga centers, and other fitness-related clubs. But many former members may never opt to renew their expensive gym passes. The fitness industry has been disrupted and consumers are finding more economical, time-efficient ways to meet their fitness needs— enter Peloton,\" Stifel explained.</p><p>\"Moving into 2021 we think measured product launches and increasing international traction will carry estimates higher over time,\" Stifel said</p><h2><strong>6. <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/w-stock\">Wayfair</a></strong></h2><p>\"Wayfair has benefited from increased spending on home categories as the pandemic has sparked housing turnover, increased nesting and forced a high degree of work/learn from home,\" Stifel explained, adding that it faces a tougher road ahead of all the other names.</p><p>\"Facing difficult compares in 2021, and having to produce heightened results against a backdrop of waning benefits from the short term factors of work/learn from home, the surge in housing turnover, and return primarily of offline (and online) competition could prove challenging. Our below consensus 2021 estimates still produce six 2019 holiday quarters. We do believe Wayfair will permanently benefit to some degree from the pandemic given the acceleration in the home category online,\" Stifel said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original I thought I had muted the Zoom video.\"</p><p>Toobin, one of the country's most prominent legal journalists, has long been a leading figure for deciphering Supreme Court arguments and decisions for height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 11 Nov 2020 22:24:00 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5fac63ae7f8f4200182a6674?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"810cbc6af58d0cab6bf4f7ff8d51a2ab","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn6@2020_2/2020/11/12/04-49-51-657_6a8ff1b8d4664238.webp","destWidth":3564,"destHeight":2673,"sourceBytes":670606,"destBytes":670606,"author":"insider@insider.com (John L. Dorman)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fac63ae7f8f4200182a6674?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn6@2020_2/2020/11/12/04-49-51-657_6a8ff1b8d4664238.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn11@2020_1/2020/11/12/04-50-05-069_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=lV4OhEb53O0:P9_zk8eW-oE:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn35@2020_3/2020/11/12/04-50-07-971_178abc00f7c572e2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=lV4OhEb53O0:P9_zk8eW-oE:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn19@2020_2/2020/11/12/04-49-55-961_7d89bd95a48a2f46.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn48@2020_5/2020/11/12/04-49-59-767_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=lV4OhEb53O0:P9_zk8eW-oE:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn55@2020_4/2020/11/12/04-50-04-574_2c4b8d5140ef8b06.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/lV4OhEb53O0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn95@2020_5/2020/11/12/04-50-03-455_76c37ee56cf4490b.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605156579248},{"createdTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:39","updatedTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:39","title":"What is liquidity? It's how easily you can sell an asset for cash — here's when and why it matters to your finances","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-liquidity","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa98a86f7d1cb0019e3a942?format=jpeg\" alt=\"liquidity\" height=\"1500\" width=\"3000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>As a measure of cash or the ability to raise it promptly, liquidity is a sign of financial health.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Photo by Supoj Buranaprapapong/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Liquidity refers to how much cash is readily available, or how quickly something can be converted to cash.</li>\n<li>Market liquidity applies to how easy it is to sell an investment &#8212; how big and constant a market there is for it.</li>\n<li>Accounting liquidity refers to the amount of ready money a company has on hand; investors use it to gauge a firm's financial health.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\"><strong>Visit Business Insider's Investing Reference library for more stories</strong></a><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\"><strong>.</strong></a></li>\n</ul><p>Liquidity may take on a different meaning depending on the context, but it always has to do with one thing: cash, or ready money.&#160;</p><p>Liquidity refers to the amount of money that is promptly available to meet debts or to use for investment. It indicates the levels of cash available and how quickly a financial asset or security can be converted into cash without losing significant value. In other words, how long it takes to sell.&#160;</p><p>Liquidity is important because it shows how flexible a company is in meeting its financial obligations and unexpected costs. It also applies to the average individual as well. The greater their liquid assets (cash savings and investment portfolio) compared to their debts, the better their financial situation.</p><h2>Types of liquidity</h2><p>Liquidity comes in two basic forms: market liquidity, which applies to investments and assets, and accounting liquidity, which applies to corporate or personal finances.</p><h3>Market liquidity</h3><p>Market liquidity refers to the liquidity of an asset and how quickly it can be turned into cash. In effect, how marketable it is, at prices that are stable and transparent.&#160;</p><p>High market liquidity means that there is a high supply and a high demand for an asset and that there will always be sellers and buyers for that asset. If someone wants to sell an asset yet there is no one to buy it, then it cannot be liquid.&#160;</p><p>Liquidity is not the same thing as profitability. Shares of a publicly traded company, for example, are liquid: They can be sold quickly on a stock exchange, even if they have dropped in value. There will always be someone to buy them.&#160;</p><p>When investing, it is important for an investor to bear in mind the liquidity of a particular asset or security. Among investments and financial vehicles, the most liquid assets include:</p><ul><li>Savings/money market accounts</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-are-blue-chip-stocks\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Stocks traded on major exchanges</a> and exchange-traded funds</li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-buy-treasury-bonds\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">US government bonds</a></li><li>Commercial paper</li><li>Other short-term money-market securities</li></ul><p>These all can be sold quickly at their fair value in return for cash.&#160;</p><p>Examples of illiquid assets, or those that can not be converted to cash quickly, tend to be tangible things, like real estate and fine art. They also include securities that trade on foreign stock exchanges, or <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-are-penny-stocks\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">penny stocks</a>, which trade over the counter.&#160;</p><p>These items all take a long time to sell.</p><h3>Accounting liquidity</h3><p>Accounting liquidity refers to a company's or a person's ability to meet their financial obligations — aka the money they owe on an ongoing basis.&#160;</p><p>With individuals, figuring liquidity is a matter of comparing their debts to the amount of cash they have in the bank or the marketable securities in their investment accounts.&#160;</p><p>With companies, it gets a tad more complex. Liquidity takes a look at a company's current assets versus its current liabilities.</p><h2>Why liquidity is important</h2><p>The higher their liquidity, the better the financial health of a business or a person is.&#160;</p><p>For example, say a company had a monthly loan payment of $5,000. Its sales are doing well and the company is realizing profits. It has no issues in meeting its $5,000 monthly obligation.</p><p>Now say the economy suffered a sudden economic downturn. Demand for the business's products has vanished so, therefore, it is not bringing in revenue and making profits; however, it still has to meet its $5,000 monthly loan bill.&#160;</p><p>Unfortunately, the company only has $3,000 of cash on hand and no liquid assets to quickly sell for cash. It will default on its loan within one month. Now if the company had $10,000 in cash and other liquid assets worth $15,000 that it could sell in a few days for cash, it would be able to meet its debt obligations for many months to come, hopefully until the economy rebounds.&#160;</p><p>The same holds for human beings. The more savings an individual has the easier it is for them to pay their debts, such as their mortgage, car loan, or credit card bills. This particularly rings true if the individual loses their job and immediate source of new income. The more cash they have on hand and more liquid assets they can sell for cash, the easier it will be for them to continue to make their debt payments while they look for a new job.</p><h2>Determining a company's liquidity</h2><p>Three liquidity ratios are primarily used to measure a company's accounting liquidity:</p><ul><li>Current ratio</li><li>Quick ratio</li><li>Cash ratio</li></ul><h3>Current ratio basics</h3><p>The current ratio, also known as the working capital ratio,&#160;seeks to determine a company's ability to meet its short-term obligations that are due within a year. It is calculated as:</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa97fc4f7d1cb0019e3a8f3?format=jpeg\" alt=\"the current or working capital ratio\" height=\"719\" width=\"1668\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The current ratio is one of the simplest liquidity measures.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Shayanne Gal/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>The higher the ratio, the better a company's financial health is and the stronger its ability to meet its financial obligations.</p><p>For example, if a company has current assets of $3 million and current liabilities of $2 million, it will have a current ratio of 3/2 = 1.5. Now, if it has current assets of $8 million and current liabilities remain at $2 million, it will have a current ratio of 8/2 = 4.&#160;</p><h3>Quick ratio basics</h3><p>The quick ratio, aka the acid test ratio, also measures current assets against current liabilities.&#160;</p><p>However, in its calculation of current assets, it only uses the most liquid assets: cash, marketable securities, and accounts receivable. It does not include inventory, which the current ratio does, as inventory cannot be sold as quickly as the other assets.</p><p>There are actually two formulas for the quick ratio:</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa97fda1df1d500182199c5?format=jpeg\" alt=\"the 2 quick ratios\" height=\"1354\" width=\"1668\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Quick ratios limit what&#39;s considered in calculating liquidity.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Shayanne Gal/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Again, the higher the ratio, the better a company is situated to meet its financial obligations.</p><h3>Cash ratio basics</h3><p>The cash ratio is an even more stringent ratio than the quick ratio. It compares <em>only </em>cash to current liabilities. If a company can meet its financial obligations through just cash without the need to sell any other assets, it is an extremely strong financial position.</p><p>The cash ratio is calculated as:</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5fa97fe7f7d1cb0019e3a8f6?format=jpeg\" alt=\"the cash ratio\" height=\"719\" width=\"1667\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The cash ratio applies the strictest standard to liquidity.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Shayanne Gal/Business Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>What liquidity ratios can tell you</h2><p>A company's liquidity can be a key factor in deciding whether to invest in its stock or buy its corporate bonds.</p><p>High liquidity ratios indicate a company is on a strong financial footing to pay its debt. Low liquidity ratios indicate that a company has a higher likelihood of defaulting, particularly if there is a downturn in its specific market or the overall economy.</p><p>Whatever the ratio you're using:&#160;</p><ul><li>A value of 1 indicates that a company has current assets equal to current liabilities.&#160;</li><li>A value above 1 indicates that a company has more current assets than current liabilities.&#160;</li><li>A value below 1 indicates that a company has more current liabilities than current assets and is not in a position to meet its financial obligations.&#160;</li></ul><p>(For the cash ratio the values would relate to just cash as opposed to all current assets.)</p><p>When comparing liquidity ratios, it is important to only compare companies within the same industry. This is because every type of industry is going to have different asset and debt requirements.</p><p>For example, a technology company does not operate the same as an airline company. The tech firm might need to buy computers and office space, while an airline needs to buy planes, a large labor force, and jet fuel. So it's natural for an airline company to carry higher levels of debt.</p><p>Financial analyst reports on companies often include liquidity ratios. Otherwise, an investor might have to calculate it themselves, using the info reported on a company's financial statements or in its annual report.</p><h2>The financial takeaway</h2><p>Liquidity refers to the amount of money an individual or corporation has on hand and the ability to quickly convert assets into cash. The higher the liquidity, the easier it is to meet financial obligations, whether you're a business or a human being.</p><p>If a person has more savings than they do debt, it means they are more financially liquid.</p><p>Companies with higher levels of cash and assets that can be readily converted to cash indicate a strong financial position as they have the ability to meet their debts and expenses, and, therefore, are better investments.&#160;</p><p>The liquidity of a particular investment is important as it indicates the level of supply and demand of that security or asset — and how quickly it can be sold for cash when needed.&#160;</p><h2>Related Coverage in&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">Investing</a>:</h2><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-volatility\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Volatility measures how dramatically stock prices change, and it can influence when, where, and how you invest</a></h3><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-diversification\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-position=\"3\" data-analytics-module=\"featured_post\">What is diversification? A portfolio strategy that uses a variety of investments to limit risk</a></h3><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-a-corporate-bond\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-position=\"6\" data-analytics-module=\"\">A corporate bond provides companies with cash and investors with income — here's how to evaluate the risks and rewards</a></h3><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/money-market-account-vs-money-market-fund\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-position=\"42\" data-analytics-module=\"\">The key differences between a money market account and a money market fund, and how they each serve different financial needs</a></h3><h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/etf-vs-mutual-fund\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-position=\"37\" data-analytics-module=\"\">ETFs and mutual funds can instantly diversify your portfolio, but they differ in how they're traded, managed, and taxed.
